‚ÄúThis year we should make the dream of a college education more attainable by tackling the difficult issue of rising student debt.‚Äù
‚ÄúWe should also work together to join the rest of the nation and raise the threshold for felony larceny...		There is no excuse for the criminal act of theft, but a teenager who steals one used iPhone or a pair of boots should not have her entire life defined by that one mistake.‚Äù
‚ÄúMy team and I will continue that policy over the next four years so that men and women who make mistakes and serve their time can reenter society as full partners in our democracy, not second-class citizens.‚Äù
‚ÄúOn the first day of this session, Governor McAuliffe spoke to you about the importance of second chances in our criminal justice system.		I was proud to stand beside him as he made history by restoring more civil rights to former offenders than any governor in American history.‚Äù
‚ÄúWe can invest the significant revenues Clean Energy Virginia will generate to create clean energy jobs in rural communities, help families lower their electrical bills, and solidify our position as a global leader in renewable energy.‚Äù
‚ÄúI will also support a bill this session that will allow us to take full advantage of this process by joining a coalition of states called the Regional Greenhouse Gas Initiative, or RGGI.‚Äù
‚ÄúThe Clean Energy Virginia initiative is an incredible opportunity to create the next generation of energy jobs and lead the fight against climate change -- and my administration will implement it fully.‚Äù
‚ÄúLast year, Governor McAuliffe signed an Executive Directive to begin the process of capping carbon emissions from Virginia‚Äôs electric utilities and use the power of the market to foster growth and innovation in the clean energy sector.‚Äù
‚ÄúAs a native of the Eastern Shore, a scientist, and a resident of Hampton Roads, I can tell you personally that, no matter what politicians in Washington say, climate change is real.	 	Sea levels are rising.	 	It affects us every day.‚Äù
‚ÄúLet‚Äôs reverse that troubling trend by passing no-excuse absentee voting, so more people can have a say in their future without jumping through unnecessary hoops.‚Äù
‚ÄúUnfortunately, Virginia law imposes many onerous and unnecessary restrictions on voting that discourage participation for many people.‚Äù
‚ÄúVoting is the most fundamental action a citizen can take in a democracy.	 	Choosing leaders and holding them accountable is how citizens shape the future for all of us.‚Äù
‚ÄúAs we begin our work, let‚Äôs ensure that all Virginians can realize their potential, no matter who they are, where they live, or whom they love.‚Äù
‚ÄúThis Commonwealth is home to people from every corner of the globe, every faith tradition, every political perspective and every income level.	 	We are also home to people who too often face discrimination or unnecessary obstacles to equality.‚Äù
‚ÄúBuilding a better Virginia for everyone means embracing and leveraging the incredible diversity of the people who live here.‚Äù
‚ÄúWe must act together this year to keep guns out of the hands of people who should not have them.‚Äù
‚ÄúAs long as the people who sent us all here continue to cry out for solutions to the epidemic of gun violence, we will fight on this ground.‚Äù
‚ÄúAs long as schools, churches, offices and concert venues are exposed to horrific, preventable violence, we will fight on this ground.‚Äù
‚ÄúAs long as Virginians‚Äô lives are at risk because there are too many guns in the hands of people who would use them to harm others, we will fight on this ground.‚Äù
‚ÄúThis issue is not a new one for the General Assembly ‚Äì but this is a new General Assembly.	 	There are many actions we should take over our time together to save lives by reducing gun violence.‚Äù
‚ÄúThis year, let‚Äôs work together to repeal limitations on a woman‚Äôs right to make her own health care decisions and please help me expand access to Long-Acting Reversible Contraceptives	 	We should also work together this year to address the public health crisis of gun violence.‚Äù
‚ÄúQuality and affordable women‚Äôs health care is a constitutional right and an economic imperative ‚Äì it is also a personal decision.‚Äù
‚ÄúAs we work to expand health coverage, we should also make it easier for Virginia women to access reproductive health care, and oppose any effort to make it harder.‚Äù
‚ÄúExpanding Medicaid is the best way for us to make life better for Virginians and truly open a new era of policymaking in the Commonwealth of Virginia.	 	Let‚Äôs get it done this year.‚Äù

‚ÄúThese men and women are not living the lives they deserve.	 	They are not making their fullest contribution to their communities or our economy.	 	But they can be.‚Äù
‚ÄúEvery single Virginian you meet is someone‚Äôs son or daughter, and many tell tales of the daily agony they experience dealing with preventable health challenges.‚Äù

‚ÄúMedicaid expansion is an opportunity to bring our tax dollars home and transform the lives of nearly 400,000 people who lack coverage today...		...As a physician, I believe that expanding Medicaid is a matter of basic economic justice.‚Äù
‚ÄúI am committed to working with the men and women of the General Assembly to expand Medicaid this year.‚Äù
‚ÄúWe are in the midst of a revolution with respect to how we research, prevent and treat a range of conditions that have historically cost too many people their productivity or even their lives.	 	I want VA to lead that revolution and to reap the economic benefits it will bring.‚Äù
‚ÄúEducation is a key predictor of a person‚Äôs prospects for lifetime success.	 	And so is health care.‚Äù
‚ÄúFinally, as we build an education system that prepares every child to succeed, we should make sure schools have the resources to educate students with special needs or learning disabilities.‚Äù
‚ÄúThe introduced budget includes more than $500 million in new funding for school divisions across VA...which will help these schools empower at-risk students to keep pace with their peers across VA, so that every child can enter the workforce ready to succeed on day one.‚Äù
‚ÄúAs we work to attract the best educators and staff on the planet, we should also recognize that a child‚Äôs prospects for lifetime success are far too often determined by the school they attend.‚Äù
‚ÄúQuality teachers are critical to educational success. So are school support staff...		These men and women play an essential role in the education of our young people and we should make sure every school can hire the best.‚Äù
‚ÄúWe should also work together now and in the years to come to make Virginia a leader in teacher pay -- so that the best and brightest come to our schools and stay for their entire careers.‚Äù
‚ÄúVirginia is home to some of the best schools on Earth ‚Äì and we should strive every day to make them better.	 	But we are also home to schools that struggle.	 	One of the most urgent reasons that some schools are falling behind is a nationwide shortage of qualified educators.‚Äù
‚ÄúBuilding a better Virginia for every family starts with offering every single child a world-class education, no matter who they are or where they live.‚Äù
‚ÄúIf we work together, we can build on our advantages in workforce development and make sure every Virginian can get the training she needs to build a successful career right at home.‚Äù
‚ÄúI hope you will accept the proposal in the introduced budget to increase funding for the New Virginia Economy Workforce Credential Grant Program...		Since its inception, this program has helped Virginians attain 4,595 industry credentials. More than 90% have gotten a job.‚Äù
‚ÄúThe centerpiece of that agenda is a plan to pay tuition and fees for any Virginian who pursues a credential in a high-demand field, if they commit to at least one year of public service.‚Äù
‚ÄúWe are also beginning the work to implement a proposal I made during the campaign called G3, which is short for Get Skilled, Get a Job, and Give Back.‚Äù
‚ÄúIf we are going to make Virginia work better for everyone, strengthening our workforce development system and expanding access to registered apprenticeships are key.‚Äù
‚ÄúI am committed to working with you to create more opportunities for Virginia workers to get a good job that empowers them to provide for their families and lead productive lives.‚Äù
‚ÄúTonight, I will lay out an agenda designed to reinforce the things that are working, and to fix the things that aren‚Äôt.	 	If we take these steps, we will answer the charge our voters gave us to make VA work better for everyone, no matter who they are or where they are from.‚Äù
‚ÄúFor many people, this is the best place on earth to live and work.	 	But while so many Virginians share in the opportunity and prosperity of a thriving state, those benefits have eluded too many of our neighbors for too long.‚Äù
‚ÄúThose of you who know me, know the Eastern Shore shaped who I am.		It‚Äôs a quiet place. A place of humility.		It‚Äôs a place where they teach the old lessons, the ones about loving our neighbor as ourselves.		And it‚Äôs a place that reminds us of Virginia‚Äôs contradictions.‚Äù
‚ÄúIn an era of social media and cable news, in a building filled with advocates, partisans and pundits, staying on the right path can be difficult.‚Äù
‚ÄúThat is a simple statement.	 	But far too often, public servants with the best of intentions find themselves pushed and pulled by forces that do not align with that goal.‚Äù
